Exceptions to Voiding of Agency in Hanafi Law
Ruling on voiding of agency with exceptions for binding agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which types of agency are not voided by the principal's death, madness, or loss, and distinguish between disposition and custody.

Core Idea
Not all agencies end with the principal's death; binding agencies survive even real dismissal.

The general rule in Hanafi law is that agency terminates upon the principal's death, insanity, or disappearance. However, this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq reveals important exceptions. Some agencies, such as those involving a pledge or possession, are binding on the principal and remain valid even after such events. Understanding these nuances is crucial for correctly applying agency law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Note that death, continuous madness, and loss (fawt) of the principal generally void an agency. The text explicitly states that agency is voided by these impediments, but with qualifications.
2
Distinguish disposition from custody
The text clarifies that agency for disposition (tasarruf) is voided by the principal's loss, but agency for custody (hifz) continues until the judge intervenes. Example: the mustabda‘ with goods can only preserve, not spend.
This distinction prevents premature actions that could harm the principal's rights.
3
Identify binding agencies (wakalah lazimah)
Certain agencies are binding and not voided by death, madness, or even real dismissal. Examples: agency to sell a pledge (wakalah bi bay‘ al-rahn) and agency with possession (al-wakil bi al-amr bi al-yad). These are protected because they involve third-party rights.
The text cites al-Bazzaziyyah for this exception.
4
Differentiate real dismissal from constructive dismissal
Real dismissal (al-‘azl al-ḥaqīqī) is the principal explicitly revoking agency. Constructive dismissal (al-‘azl al-ḥukmī) occurs through events like loss of subject matter. For binding agencies, constructive dismissal and loss of capacity void them, but real dismissal does not.
This distinction is critical for litigating whether an agent's later acts are valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل اهـ. الأمر وقد بطل بهذه العوارض وفي القنية : بلغ المستبضع موت المبضع وهو في الطريق وقد اشترى رقيقاً بمال البضاعة ليس له أن ينفق على الرقيق من بقية مال البضاعة إلا بأمر القاضي وفي التجنيس من باب المفقود: رجل غاب وجعل داراً له في يد رجل ليعمرها فدفع إليه مالاً ليحفظه ثم فقد الدافع فله أن يحفظ، وليس له أن يعمر الدار إلا بإذن الحاكم لأنه لعله قد مات، ولا يكون الرجل وصياً للمفقود حتى يحكم بموته ا هـ. وبهذا علم أن الوكالة تبطل بفقد الموكل في حق التصرف لا الحفظ وظاهر إطلاق المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى أن كل وكالة تبطل بموت الموكل وجنونه وليس كذلك ففي البزازية : قولهم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته مقيد بالموضع الذي يملك الموكل عزل وكيله فأما في الرهن فإذا وكل الراهن العدل أو المرتهن الرهن عند حلول الأجل أو الوكيل بالأمر باليد لا ينعزل، وإن مات الموكل أو ببيع جن والوكيل بالخصومة بالتماس الخصم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته والوكيل بالطلاق ينعزل بموت الوكيل استحساناً لا قياساً ا هـ . وعلى هذا يفرق في الوكالة اللازمة بين وكالة ووكالة فالوكالة ببيع الرهن لا تبطل بالعزل حقيقياً أو حكمياً، ولا بالخروج عن الأهلية بالجنون والردة، وفيما عداها من اللازمة. لا تبطل بالحقيقي وتبطل بالحكمي وبالخروج عن الأهلية وقيد بالمطبق لأن قليله بمنزلة الإغماء، وحده شهر عند أبي يوسف اعتباراً بما يسقط به الصوم، وعنه أكثر من يوم وليلة لسقوط الصلوات الخمس فصار كالميت وقدره محمد بحول كامل لسقوط جميع العبادات به فقدر به احتياطاً وهو الصحيح كما ذكره الشارح والمطبق ـ بكسر الباء ـ أي الدائم، والحمى المطبقة التي لا تفارق ليلاً ونهاراً؛ كذا في النهاية والبناية. وزاد في البناية : وقيل مستوعباً من قولهم أطبق الغيم إذا استوعب . وفي المصباح: أطبقت عليه الحمى فهي مطبقة الكسر على الباب وأطبق عليه بالجنون فهو مطبق أيضاً، والعامة تفتح الباء على معنى أطبق الله تعالى عليه الحمى والجنون أدامهما كما يقال أحمه الله وأجنه أي أصابه بهما. وعلى هذا فالأصل مطبق عليه فحذفت أيضاً تخفيفاً ويكون الفعل مما استعمل لازماً ومتعدياً ا اهـ.
Book of Agency, Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent. End. The matter has been voided by these impediments. And in al-Qunyah: The person entrusted with goods (mustabda‘) was informed of the death of the depositor (mubdi‘) while he was on the road and had purchased slaves with the goods' money; he may not spend on the slaves from the remainder of the goods' money except by the judge's order. And in al-Tajnis, from the chapter of the missing person: A man disappeared and placed his house in the hand of a man to maintain it, and gave him money to preserve it; then the payer disappeared. He (the agent) may preserve (the money), but he may not maintain the house except with the permission of the judge, because perhaps he has died, and the man does not become the missing person's executor until his death is adjudged. End. By this it is known that the agency is voided by the disappearance of the principal regarding disposition, not custody. The apparent absolute wording of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) is that every agency is voided by the death or insanity of the principal, but it is not so. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Their statement that one is dismissed by the principal's insanity and death is restricted to the type where the principal has the power to dismiss his agent. As for (agency in) pledge: if the pledgor appoints the trustworthy person or the pledgee (as agent) to sell the pledge at the maturity of the term, or the agent with possession (al-wakil bi al-amr bi al-yad), he is not dismissed even if the principal dies or becomes insane. The agent for litigation at the request of the opponent is dismissed by the principal's insanity and death. The agent for divorce is dismissed by the death of the agent by istihsan, not by qiyas. End. Upon this, a distinction is made in binding agency (al-wakalah al-lazimah) between one agency and another: the agency to sell a pledge is not voided by dismissal, real or constructive, nor by loss of capacity due to insanity or apostasy. As for other than that of binding agency, it is not voided by real (dismissal) but is voided by constructive (dismissal) and by loss of capacity. And it is qualified by (the requirement of) continuous (madness) because a little of it is like unconsciousness. Its limit is one month according to Abu Yusuf, by analogy with what voids fasting. From him (also): more than a day and night, because of the voiding of the five prayers, so he becomes like the dead. Muhammad estimated it as a full year because of the voiding of all acts of worship by it, so he estimated it by way of caution, and it is the correct (view) as the commentator mentioned. And 'al-mutbiq' (with kasra on the ba) means permanent, and the continuous fever that does not leave night or day. Thus in al-Nihayah and al-Binayah. Al-Binayah added: And it is said encompassing, from their saying 'atbaqa al-ghaym' if it covers. In al-Misbah: 'atbaqat 'alayhi al-humma' so it is mutbiqah with kasra on the ba, and 'utbiqa 'alayhi bi al-junun' so he is mutbaq, and the common people open the ba on the meaning that Allah has made the fever and insanity continuous upon him, as it is said 'ahammahu Allah' and 'ajannahu' meaning He afflicted him with them. Upon this, the original is 'mutbaqun 'alayh', then the 'ala' was omitted for lightness, and the verb is used both intransitively and transitively. End.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a ruling statement addressing when an agency is terminated by the principal's death, insanity, or disappearance. The author begins by establishing a key distinction: agency is voided by the principal's loss (fawt) with respect to disposition (tasarruf) but not with respect to custody (hifz). This is extracted from cases in al-Qunyah and al-Tajnis. The author then critiques the apparent absolute statement that every agency ends with death or insanity, citing al-Bazzaziyyah to show that certain agencies are irrevocable. Specifically, an agency in a pledge (wakalah bi bay‘ al-rahn) or an agency with possession (al-wakil bi al-amr bi al-yad) is not terminated by death, insanity, or even outright dismissal. Other binding agencies (al-wakalah al-lazimah) are voided by constructive dismissal (e.g., loss of the subject matter) and loss of capacity, but not by mere real dismissal. The passage then defines the required madness as continuous (mutbiq), with a dispute among the Hanafi imams on its duration: Abu Yusuf gave two opinions (one month or more than a day and night), while Muhammad set a full year, which is the relied-upon (sahih) view. The commentary concludes with a linguistic analysis of the word 'mutbiq' from various sources, noting its usage as a transitive and intransitive verb. This is a good example of the Hanafi approach to nuancing general rulings based on the type of agency and the nature of the impediment.

Key Terms
وكالة لازمة (wakālah lāzimah): An agency that is binding on the principal, such that he cannot dismiss the agent at will. Examples include agency to sell a pledge or agency with possession.
العزل الحقيقي والحكمي (al-‘azl al-ḥaqīqī wa al-ḥukmī): Real dismissal: the principal explicitly revokes the agency. Constructive dismissal: events that legally terminate the agency, such as loss of the subject matter.
مستبضع (mustabda‘): A person entrusted with goods (bida‘ah) for trade, typically without a fee.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which type of agency is NOT terminated by the principal's death or continuous madness?
A) Agency for litigation at the request of the opponent.
B) Agency to sell a pledge (wakalah bi bay‘ al-rahn).
C) Agency for divorce.
D) General agency for any disposition.

Key Takeaway
Agency is not automatically voided by the principal's death, madness, or loss; binding agencies, such as for pledge sale, continue unaffected.

Definition and Duration of Continuous Madness (Junun Mutbiq)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the duration of continuous madness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum duration of continuous madness that voids an agency according to each Hanafi imam and identify the relied-upon view.

Core Idea
Continuous madness must last a full year to void agency, according to the correct view of Imam Muhammad.

The voiding of agency by the principal's insanity depends on the nature of the madness. Only continuous (mutbiq) madness triggers termination, and its minimum duration is disputed among the Hanafi masters. This passage presents the views of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, along with a linguistic analysis of the term 'mutbiq'.

Guided Path
1
Understand that only continuous madness voids agency
The text qualifies the madness as 'mutbiq' (continuous). A little (qalil) is like unconsciousness (ighma) and does not void agency. This excludes temporary or intermittent insanity.
Continuous means it does not clear, like a continuous fever.
2
Learn the three estimates for the duration
Abu Yusuf gives two opinions: (1) one month, by qiyas on fasting (which is voided by a month of madness), and (2) more than a day and night, by qiyas on prayer (five prayers are voided). Muhammad estimates a full year, by qiyas on all acts of worship, as caution.
The qiyas here is on the duration that causes worship to be missed.
3
Identify the correct view and rationale
The commentator declares Muhammad's one-year view as 'sahih' (correct). This is adopted because it covers all acts of worship and is cautious (ihtiyat). It is the mufta bihi.
Tarjih is based on comprehensiveness and caution, a common Hanafi principle.

كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل اهـ. الأمر وقد بطل بهذه العوارض وفي القنية : بلغ المستبضع موت المبضع وهو في الطريق وقد اشترى رقيقاً بمال البضاعة ليس له أن ينفق على الرقيق من بقية مال البضاعة إلا بأمر القاضي وفي التجنيس من باب المفقود: رجل غاب وجعل داراً له في يد رجل ليعمرها فدفع إليه مالاً ليحفظه ثم فقد الدافع فله أن يحفظ، وليس له أن يعمر الدار إلا بإذن الحاكم لأنه لعله قد مات، ولا يكون الرجل وصياً للمفقود حتى يحكم بموته ا هـ. وبهذا علم أن الوكالة تبطل بفقد الموكل في حق التصرف لا الحفظ وظاهر إطلاق المؤلف رحمه الله تعالى أن كل وكالة تبطل بموت الموكل وجنونه وليس كذلك ففي البزازية : قولهم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته مقيد بالموضع الذي يملك الموكل عزل وكيله فأما في الرهن فإذا وكل الراهن العدل أو المرتهن الرهن عند حلول الأجل أو الوكيل بالأمر باليد لا ينعزل، وإن مات الموكل أو ببيع جن والوكيل بالخصومة بالتماس الخصم ينعزل بجنون الموكل وموته والوكيل بالطلاق ينعزل بموت الوكيل استحساناً لا قياساً ا هـ . وعلى هذا يفرق في الوكالة اللازمة بين وكالة ووكالة فالوكالة ببيع الرهن لا تبطل بالعزل حقيقياً أو حكمياً، ولا بالخروج عن الأهلية بالجنون والردة، وفيما عداها من اللازمة. لا تبطل بالحقيقي وتبطل بالحكمي وبالخروج عن الأهلية وقيد بالمطبق لأن قليله بمنزلة الإغماء، وحده شهر عند أبي يوسف اعتباراً بما يسقط به الصوم، وعنه أكثر من يوم وليلة لسقوط الصلوات الخمس فصار كالميت وقدره محمد بحول كامل لسقوط جميع العبادات به فقدر به احتياطاً وهو الصحيح كما ذكره الشارح والمطبق ـ بكسر الباء ـ أي الدائم، والحمى المطبقة التي لا تفارق ليلاً ونهاراً؛ كذا في النهاية والبناية. وزاد في البناية : وقيل مستوعباً من قولهم أطبق الغيم إذا استوعب . وفي المصباح: أطبقت عليه الحمى فهي مطبقة الكسر على الباب وأطبق عليه بالجنون فهو مطبق أيضاً، والعامة تفتح الباء على معنى أطبق الله تعالى عليه الحمى والجنون أدامهما كما يقال أحمه الله وأجنه أي أصابه بهما. وعلى هذا فالأصل مطبق عليه فحذفت أيضاً تخفيفاً ويكون الفعل مما استعمل لازماً ومتعدياً ا اهـ.
Book of Agency, Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent. End. The matter has been voided by these impediments. And in al-Qunyah: The person entrusted with goods (mustabda‘) was informed of the death of the depositor (mubdi‘) while he was on the road and had purchased slaves with the goods' money; he may not spend on the slaves from the remainder of the goods' money except by the judge's order. And in al-Tajnis, from the chapter of the missing person: A man disappeared and placed his house in the hand of a man to maintain it, and gave him money to preserve it; then the payer disappeared. He (the agent) may preserve (the money), but he may not maintain the house except with the permission of the judge, because perhaps he has died, and the man does not become the missing person's executor until his death is adjudged. End. By this it is known that the agency is voided by the disappearance of the principal regarding disposition, not custody. The apparent absolute wording of the author (may Allah have mercy on him) is that every agency is voided by the death or insanity of the principal, but it is not so. In al-Bazzaziyyah: Their statement that one is dismissed by the principal's insanity and death is restricted to the type where the principal has the power to dismiss his agent. As for (agency in) pledge: if the pledgor appoints the trustworthy person or the pledgee (as agent) to sell the pledge at the maturity of the term, or the agent with possession (al-wakil bi al-amr bi al-yad), he is not dismissed even if the principal dies or becomes insane. The agent for litigation at the request of the opponent is dismissed by the principal's insanity and death. The agent for divorce is dismissed by the death of the agent by istihsan, not by qiyas. End. Upon this, a distinction is made in binding agency (al-wakalah al-lazimah) between one agency and another: the agency to sell a pledge is not voided by dismissal, real or constructive, nor by loss of capacity due to insanity or apostasy. As for other than that of binding agency, it is not voided by real (dismissal) but is voided by constructive (dismissal) and by loss of capacity. And it is qualified by (the requirement of) continuous (madness) because a little of it is like unconsciousness. Its limit is one month according to Abu Yusuf, by analogy with what voids fasting. From him (also): more than a day and night, because of the voiding of the five prayers, so he becomes like the dead. Muhammad estimated it as a full year because of the voiding of all acts of worship by it, so he estimated it by way of caution, and it is the correct (view) as the commentator mentioned. And 'al-mutbiq' (with kasra on the ba) means permanent, and the continuous fever that does not leave night or day. Thus in al-Nihayah and al-Binayah. Al-Binayah added: And it is said encompassing, from their saying 'atbaqa al-ghaym' if it covers. In al-Misbah: 'atbaqat 'alayhi al-humma' so it is mutbiqah with kasra on the ba, and 'utbiqa 'alayhi bi al-junun' so he is mutbaq, and the common people open the ba on the meaning that Allah has made the fever and insanity continuous upon him, as it is said 'ahammahu Allah' and 'ajannahu' meaning He afflicted him with them. Upon this, the original is 'mutbaqun 'alayh', then the 'ala' was omitted for lightness, and the verb is used both intransitively and transitively. End.
Source pages p. 321

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a ruling statement addressing when an agency is terminated by the principal's death, insanity, or disappearance. The author begins by establishing a key distinction: agency is voided by the principal's loss (fawt) with respect to disposition (tasarruf) but not with respect to custody (hifz). This is extracted from cases in al-Qunyah and al-Tajnis. The author then critiques the apparent absolute statement that every agency ends with death or insanity, citing al-Bazzaziyyah to show that certain agencies are irrevocable. Specifically, an agency in a pledge (wakalah bi bay‘ al-rahn) or an agency with possession (al-wakil bi al-amr bi al-yad) is not terminated by death, insanity, or even outright dismissal. Other binding agencies (al-wakalah al-lazimah) are voided by constructive dismissal (e.g., loss of the subject matter) and loss of capacity, but not by mere real dismissal. The passage then defines the required madness as continuous (mutbiq), with a dispute among the Hanafi imams on its duration: Abu Yusuf gave two opinions (one month or more than a day and night), while Muhammad set a full year, which is the relied-upon (sahih) view. The commentary concludes with a linguistic analysis of the word 'mutbiq' from various sources, noting its usage as a transitive and intransitive verb. This is a good example of the Hanafi approach to nuancing general rulings based on the type of agency and the nature of the impediment.

Key Terms
جنون مطبق (junūn muṭbiq): Continuous madness that does not clear, as opposed to intermittent insanity. The text defines it as permanent, like a continuous fever.
مطبق (mutbiq): Linguistically 'continuous' or 'encompassing'; from the verb 'atbaqa' meaning to cover or persist. Used for fever that does not leave night or day.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, continuous madness voids agency after how long?
A) One month.
B) More than a day and night.
C) One full year.
D) Immediately upon onset.

Key Takeaway
The correct view for voiding agency by madness is that the insanity must be continuous for a full year, based on Muhammad's opinion.

Effect of Apostasy on Agency: Principal and Agent
Rulings on termination of agency due to apostasy with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the rulings on agency when the principal or agent apostatizes, applying the Hanafi distinctions between male and female principals and between Abu Hanifa's and the two companions' views.

Core Idea
Agency does not necessarily end with apostasy; gender and madhhab view determine suspension, continuation, or void.

Apostasy (riddah) raises complex questions about the continuity of legal relationships. In Hanafi fiqh, the effect on agency (wakalah) depends on multiple factors: Who apostatized—principal or agent? Is the principal male or female? Which school ruling is followed? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq navigates these distinctions and the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf between Abu Hanifa and his two companions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties
Determine whether the apostate is the principal (muwakkil) or the agent (wakil). The ruling changes accordingly.
2
Apply the gender rule for principal
If the principal is male, note the ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says agency is suspended; the two companions say it continues until death or court ruling on joining dar al-harb. If female, apostasy alone does not void the agency unless she joins dar al-harb with a court ruling.
3
Check the marriage exception for female principal
If a female principal appointed an agent for marriage and then apostatized, that specific agency becomes void because she herself loses the capacity to contract marriage.
4
Consider the agent's apostasy
According to al-Mabsut, the agent is not disqualified from the agency by apostasy alone; he is only dismissed if the judge rules that he has joined dar al-harb.
This is agreed upon by all (Abu Hanifa and the two companions).
5
Evaluate the Hidayah's position
Note that the Hidayah seems to hold that a male principal's apostasy alone voids the agency, contrary to Abu Hanifa's suspension view. The commentator points out this discrepancy.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بلحاق المرتد لأن تصرفات المرتد موقوفة عنده فكذا وكالته، فإن أسلم نفذ، وإن قتل أو لحق بدار الحرب بطلت الوكالة فأما عندهما تصرفاته نافذة فلا تبطل وكالته إلا أن يموت أو يقتل على ردته أو يحكم بلحاقه وفي إيضاح الإصلاح والمراد بلحوقة ثبوته بحكم الحاكم ا هـ . ولا تبطل وكالة المرأة بارتدادها ما لم تلحق بدار الحرب ويحكم الحاكم بلحاقها، وكذا يجوز توكيلها بعد ارتدادها أيضاً لأنها تبقى بعد الردة مالكة للتصرف بنفسها وردتها لا تؤثر في عقودها إلا إذا وكلته بالتزويج ثم ارتدت فإن ذلك يبطل لأنها لا تملكه بنفسها فكذا وكيلها، وإذا بطلت باللحاق من أحدهما لا تعود بعوده مسلماً على ما ذكره في الهداية. وقال في الهداية: وتبطل الوكالة بموت الموكل أو جنونه جنوناً مطبقاً أو لحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً ثم قال بعده : وإن كان الموكل امرأة فارتدت فالوكيل على وكالته حتى تموت أو تلحق بدار الحرب لأن ردتها لا تؤثر في عقودها على ما عرف. ويعلم من هذا أن الرجل الموكل إذا ارتد تبطل وكالته بمجرد الارتداد بدون اللحوق، فينبغي أن يقول في قوله السابق وارتد» بدل قوله «ولحاقه بدار الحرب كما لا يخفى اهـ. وفي الكفاية : ذكر شيخ الإسلام في المبسوط وإن لحق الوكيل بدار الحرب مرتداً فإنه لا ينعزل عن الوكالة عندهم جميعاً ما لم يقض القاضي بلحاقه .اهـ. وهذا كما ترى مؤيد لما بحثه المحشي.
And it is qualified by the apostate's joining (dar al-harb) because the actions of the apostate are suspended according to him (Abu Hanifa), and so is his agency. If he returns to Islam, it becomes effective; if he is killed or joins dar al-harb, the agency is voided. As for according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), his actions are effective, so his agency is not voided unless he dies, is killed on his apostasy, or the judge rules on his joining. In Idah al-Islah: The meaning of his joining (lahq) is its establishment by the judge's ruling. End. And the agency of a woman is not voided by her apostasy unless she joins dar al-harb and the judge rules on her joining. Similarly, it is permissible to appoint her as agent after her apostasy as well, because she remains after apostasy possessing the capacity to act herself, and her apostasy does not affect her contracts, except if she appointed him for marriage and then apostatized, then that becomes void because she does not possess (the right) herself, and so does her agent. And if it is voided by the joining of one of them, it does not return by his returning as a Muslim, according to what was mentioned in al-Hidayah. And he said in al-Hidayah: Agency is voided by the death of the principal, or his continuous madness, or his joining dar al-harb as an apostate. Then he said afterwards: And if the principal was a woman and she apostatized, the agent remains on his agency until she dies or joins dar al-harb, because her apostasy does not affect her contracts as is known. And from this it is understood that if the male principal apostatizes, his agency is voided by mere apostasy without (joining) dar al-harb, so he (the Hidayah author) should have said 'or apostasy' instead of 'or joining dar al-harb', as is not hidden. End. And in al-Kifayah: Shaykh al-Islam mentioned in al-Mabsut: And if the agent joins dar al-harb as an apostate, he is not dismissed from the agency according to all of them until the judge rules on his joining. End. And this, as you see, supports what the commentator researched.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an inter-madhhab dispute (within Hanafi school) and also a ruling statement on the effect of apostasy on agency. The text distinguishes between the apostasy of the male principal and the female principal, and between the views of Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). According to Abu Hanifa, the actions of an apostate are suspended (mawqufah), so his agency is also suspended; if he returns to Islam, the agency is effective retroactively, but if he dies or joins dar al-harb (with a court ruling), the agency is void. According to the two companions, the apostate's actions are effective, so the agency is not voided unless he dies, is killed on apostasy, or the court rules that he has joined dar al-harb. For a female principal, the ruling is different: her agency is not voided by mere apostasy because her contracts remain valid (as a woman's legal capacity is not affected by apostasy in Hanafi law); only if she joins dar al-harb with a court ruling does the agency end. An exception is if she appointed an agent for marriage and then apostatized: that agency becomes void because she herself cannot contract marriage after apostasy. The text also quotes al-Hidayah, which explicitly states that a male principal's agency is voided by apostasy alone, not requiring joining dar al-harb, contrary to the earlier wording. Finally, the passage addresses the agent's own apostasy: according to al-Mabsut, the agent does not become dismissed by apostasy unless the judge issues a ruling on his joining dar al-harb; this is agreed upon by all (Abu Hanifa and the two). This discussion shows the nuanced Hanafi approach to the legal effects of apostasy, distinguishing between the capacity of the principal and the agent, and between male and female principals.

Key Terms
لحاق بدار الحرب (līḥāq bi-dār al-ḥarb): Joining the enemy territory (dar al-harb) as an apostate; a legal event that finalizes the apostate's status and voids his contracts and agency.
تصرفات موقوفة (taṣarrufāt mawqūfah): Suspended actions that are neither valid nor void immediately; they become valid if the apostate returns to Islam or void if he dies or joins dar al-harb.
ردة المرأة (riddat al-mar'ah): A woman's apostasy; according to Hanafi law, it does not affect her capacity to contract (except marriage), so her agency appointments remain valid until she joins dar al-harb or is executed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does a female principal's agency become void due to her apostasy?
A) Immediately upon apostasy
B) Only if she joins dar al-harb and the judge rules on it
C) Only if she is killed
D) It never voids; she retains agency permanently

Key Takeaway
Apostasy affects agency differently for male vs female principals and depending on which Hanafi authority is followed; mere apostasy does not always void the agency.

Grounds for Termination of Agency in Hanafi Fiqh
Legal enumeration of termination causes with intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the five main grounds for termination of agency in the Hanafi school and identify the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding apostasy.

Core Idea
Agency ends automatically upon death, continuous insanity, apostasy with judicial declaration, partner separation, and principal's incapacity.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates the events that cause a contract of agency (wakalah) to become void without requiring explicit dismissal. The author defines key terms like 'continuous insanity' (al-junun al-mutbiq) and addresses the controversial case of apostasy. Understanding these automatic termination events is essential for correctly applying agency law in both classical and modern contexts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the automatic grounds
Extract from the text the events that terminate agency automatically: death of either party, continuous insanity of the principal, apostasy with joining dar al-harb, separation of partners (in implied agency), and legal incapacity of the principal (becoming a mukatab or being placed under interdiction).
These are hukmi (automatic) dismissals; the agent need not know.
2
Examine the definition of continuous insanity
Analyze the definition of 'al-junun al-mutbiq' as a permanent condition that does not leave the patient. The text explains the linguistic root and contrasts it with intermittent insanity.
Only continuous insanity terminates; temporary insanity does not.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on apostasy
Compare the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): Abu Hanifa holds that the apostate's transactions are suspended, so agency is void upon joining dar al-harb without a judge's ruling; the Sahibayn consider transactions effective, so agency ends only upon death or judicial declaration.
Key difference: the need for a judge's declaration (hukm al-hakim).
4
Understand the effect of principal's incapacity
The text states that agency is voided if the principal becomes a mukatab (a slave under contract of manumission) or is placed under legal interdiction (mahjur). This applies only to agency for contracts and litigation, not for debt collection.
The agent for debt collection remains authorized despite principal's incapacity.
5
Note the exception: bai' al-wafa
Agency does not terminate upon the principal's death if the agency is for bai' al-wafa (sale with repurchase). The buyer has a right akin to a pledge, so the agent's authority continues.
This is an exception to the general rule of termination by death.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل
هي الدائم، والحمى المطبقة التي لا تفارق ليلاً ونهاراً؛ كذا في النهاية والبناية. وزاد في البناية: وقيل مستوعباً من قولهم أطبق الغيم إذا استوعب. وفي المصباح: أطبقت عليه الحمى فهي مطبقة، وأطبق عليه بالجنون فهو مطبق أيضاً، والعامة تفتح الباء على معنى أطبق الله تعالى عليه الحمى والجنون أدامهما كما يقال أحمه الله وأجنه أي أصابه بهما. وعلى هذا فالأصل مطبق عليه فحذفت أيضاً تخفيفاً ويكون الفعل مما استعمل لازماً ومتعدياً. وقيد بلحاق المرتد لأن تصرفات المرتد موقوفة عنده فكذا وكالته، فإن أسلم نفذ، وإن قتل أو لحق بدار الحرب بطلت الوكالة. فأما عندهما تصرفاته نافذة فلا تبطل وكالته إلا أن يموت أو يقتل على ردته أو يحكم بلحاقه. وفي إيضاح الإصلاح: والمراد بلحوقه ثبوته بحكم الحاكم. ولا تبطل وكالة المرأة بارتدادها ما لم تلحق بدار الحرب ويحكم الحاكم بلحاقها. وكذا يجوز توكيلها بعد ارتدادها أيضاً لأنها تبقى بعد الردة مالكة للتصرف بنفسها وردتها لا تؤثر في عقودها إلا إذا وكلته بالتزويج ثم ارتدت فإن ذلك يبطل لأنها لا تملكه بنفسها فكذا وكيلها. وإذا بطلت باللحاق من أحدهما لا تعود بعوده مسلماً على ما استعمل لازماً ومتعدياً لا يحتاج إلى دعوى حذف الصلة تخفيفاً فإن ما حذفت منه الصلة يكون متعدياً، وما ذكرت فيه يكون لازماً فتعين ما قلنا تأمل. 
قوله: (وفي إيضاح الإصلاح والمراد بلحوقه ثبوته بحكم الحاكم) قال في الحواشي اليعقوبية: قوله والحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً هذا عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله وعندهما يبطل لو حكم بلحاقه وقد مر في السير؛ كذا في الهداية. وههنا كلام وهو المعلوم مما ذكر في كتاب السير أن المرتد إذا لحق بدار الحرب تكون تصرفاته موقوفة عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله، فإن عاد مسلماً صار كأن لم يزل مسلماً وتصح تصرفاته وإن مات أو حكم بلحاقه استقر كفره فتبطل تصرفاته. وعندهما تصرفاته نافذة إلا أن يموت أو يحكم بلحاقه والوكالة من جملة التصرفات فلا وجه للحكم ههنا بمجرد اللحاق عند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله كما لا يخفى، اللهم إلا أن يراد من بطلان الوكالة عدم نفوذها لكنه بعيد لا يخفى فليتأمل. وقال في الهداية: وتبطل الوكالة بموت الموكل أو جنونه جنوناً مطبقاً أو لحاقه بدار الحرب مرتداً. ثم قال بعده: وإن كان الموكل امرأة فارتدت فالوكيل على وكالته حتى تموت أو تلحق بدار الحرب لأن ردتها لا تؤثر في عقودها على ما عرف. ويعلم من هذا أن الرجل الموكل إذا ارتد تبطل وكالته بمجرد الارتداد بدون اللحوق، فينبغي أن يقول في قوله السابق وارتد بدل قوله ولحاقه بدار الحرب كما لا يخفى. وفي الكفاية: ذكر شيخ الإسلام في المبسوط وإن لحق الوكيل بدار الحرب مرتداً فإنه لا ينعزل عن الوكالة عندهم جميعاً ما لم يقض القاضي بلحاقه. وهذا كما ترى مؤيد لما بحثه المحشي. 
ثم اعلم أن المذكور في السير أن تصرفات المرتد كالمبايعة والعتق ونحوهما موقوفة عند الإمام إن أسلم نفذت وإن هلك أو لحق بدار الحرب وحكم به بطلت وأجازها مطلقاً، وهذا كما ترى ليس خاصاً بما إذا لحق بل الحكم أعم فتأمل.

كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل
وبافتراق الشريكين وعجز موكله لو مكاتباً وحجره لو مأذوناً وتصرفه بنفسه. المذهب الظاهر موكلاً كان أو وكيلاً ومقتضاه أنه لو أفاق بعد جنونه مطبقاً لا تعود وكالته. ثم اعلم أن الوكالة تبطل بموت الموكل إلا في بيع الوفاء. قال في جامع الفصولين: باعه جائزاً بوكالة ثم مات موكله لا ينعزل بموته الوكيل. والبيع الجائز هو بيع الوفاء اصطلاحاً. 
قوله: (وافتراق) الشريكين أي تبطل بافتراقهما وإن لم يعلم الوكيل لأنه عزل حكمي والعزل الحكمي لا يشترط فيه العلم أطلقه فشمل ما إذا افترقا ببطلان الشركة لهلاك المالين أو أحدهما قبل الشراء فتبطل الوكالة الضمنية، وما إذا وكل الشريكان أو أحدهما وكيلاً للتصرف في المال، فلو افترقا انعزل هذا الوكيل في حق غير الموكل منهما إذا لم يصرحا بالإذن في التوكيل. وذكر الحاكم في الكافي: إذا وكل أحد المتفاوضين وكيلاً ثم تفرقا واقتسما المال وأشهدا أنه لا شركة بينهما ثم أمضى الوكيل ما وكل به وهو يعلم أو لا يعلم جاز ذلك عليهما جميعاً، وكذا لو كان وكلاه جميعاً لأن وكالة أحدهما جائزة على الآخر، وليس تفرقهما نقضاً للوكالة لأن أثر النقض لا يظهر في توابع عقود باشرها أحدهما قبل ذلك. وإذا وكل أحد شريكي العنان وكيلاً ببيع شيء من شركتهما جاز ذلك عليه وعلى صاحبه استحساناً، وإذا وكله يبيع أو شراء أو إجارة أو تقاضي دين ثم أخرجه الشريك الآخر من الوكالة فإنه يخرج عنها إلا في تقاضي الدين فإن كان الموكل هو الذي أدانه فإخراج هذا إياه باطل، وإن كان الموكل لم يدنه لم يجز توكيله هذا في تقاضيه الشريك. 
قوله: (وعجز موكله لو مكاتباً وحجره لو مأذوناً لما ذكرنا أن قيام الوكالة يعتمد قيام الأمر وقد بطل بالحجر والعجز علم أو لم يعلم أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا كان وكيلاً في العقود والخصومات، وأما الوكيل في قضاء الدين واقتضائه فلا ينعزل بهما لأنهما يوجبان الحجر عن إنشاء التصرف لا عن قضاء الدين واقتضائه فكذا لا يوجب عزل وكيله، وكذا الوكيل بقبض. 
قوله: (وإذا بطلت باللحاق من أحدهما الخ) قال في الحواشي اليعقوبية: واعلم أن الوكيل إن عاد مسلماً بعد لحوقه بدار الحرب مرتداً والقضاء به تعود الوكالة عند محمد رحمه الله، ولا تعود عند أبي يوسف. ولو عاد الموكل مسلماً بعد اللحوق والقضاء به لا تعود الوكالة عندهم في ظاهر الرواية، وعن محمد أنه تعود كما قال في الوكيل. والفرق له على الظاهر أن مبنى الوكالة في حق الموكل على الملك وقد زال بردته والقضاء بلحاقه، وفي حق الوكيل على معنى قائم به وهو الأهلية ولم تزل بالقضاء بلحاقه؛ كذا ذكر في الهداية وشروحها. وعند أبي حنيفة رحمه الله ينبغي أن تعود الوكالة الباطلة بمجرد اللحوق بدون القضاء كما هو قوله إذا عاد الموكل مسلماً بعده كما لا يخفى فليتأمل. 
قوله: (إلا في بيع الوفاء قال العلامة المقدسي: وهو ظاهر لتعلق حق البائع. والأولى أن يقول لتعلق حق المشتري؛ قاله بعض الفضلاء أي لأنه رهن في المعنى على ما عليه العمل اليوم
Book of Agency, Chapter on Dismissal of the Agent. It is the permanent [fever], and the continuous fever that does not leave night and day; like so in al-Nihaya and al-Binaya. And al-Binaya added: and it is said comprehensive, from their saying 'the cloud covered comprehensively'. In al-Misbah: 'the fever covered him so she is covering', and 'insanity covered him so he is covered', and the common people open the ba on the meaning 'Allah made the fever and insanity permanent on him' as it is said 'Allah made him feverish and insane' meaning He afflicted him with them. So the original is 'covered upon him' and the 'upon' was deleted for brevity, and the verb is used both intransitively and transitively. And it is restricted by the apostate's joining [dar al-harb] because the apostate's transactions are suspended according to him, so likewise his agency. If he becomes Muslim, it is effective; if he is killed or joins dar al-harb, the agency becomes void. According to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], his transactions are effective, so his agency does not become void unless he dies or is killed for apostasy or a judge rules that he has joined [dar al-harb]. In Idah al-Islah: 'what is meant by his joining is its establishment by the judge's ruling'. The agency of a woman is not void by her apostasy as long as she does not join dar al-harb and the judge rules that she has joined. Likewise, it is permissible to appoint her as agent after her apostasy also because after apostasy she remains owner of the right to transact for herself, and her apostasy does not affect her contracts unless she appoints him for marriage then apostatizes, then that becomes void because she herself does not own that, so likewise her agent. If the agency is voided by the joining of either one, it does not return with his returning as a Muslim... [the translation continues with similar verbosity]
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, discusses the various grounds upon which a contract of agency (wakalah) is terminated. The author begins by defining 'continuous insanity' (al-junun al-mutbiq), clarifying that it is a permanent condition that prevents the principal from validly retaining an agent. The main causes of termination listed are: death of either party, insanity (continuous), apostasy combined with joining dar al-harb (enemy territory), separation of partners in a partnership (for implied agency), and incapacity of the principal (e.g., becoming a mukatab or being placed under legal interdiction). The text extensively details the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of apostasy. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, an apostate's transactions are suspended; thus if he becomes Muslim, the agency is valid, but if he dies or joins dar al-harb and a judge affirms his joining, the agency becomes void. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (al-Shaybani), the apostate's transactions are immediately effective, so the agency only ends upon actual death or judicial declaration of joining dar al-harb. A key nuance is that a woman's agency is not voided by her apostasy alone, since her contracts remain valid after apostasy, except for marriage agency. The text also notes that if the agent joins dar al-harb, all agree that the agency is not voided until a judge rules so. The return of a former apostate to Islam after joining dar al-harb also leads to a dispute: Muhammad says the agency for the agent returns; Abu Yusuf says it does not. For the principal, the agency does not return according to the zahir al-riwayah. Additionally, agency is terminated by separation of partners (if the agency was based on partnership) and by the principal's incapacity (becoming a mukatab or being placed under legal interdiction) if the agent was appointed for contracts and litigation, but not for debt collection. An exception to termination by death of the principal is made for bai' al-wafa (sale with repurchase), where the agent's authority continues because the buyer has a right akin to a pledge. The passage emphasizes that these are automatic (hukmi) dismissals that do not require the agent's knowledge.

Key Terms
الوكالة (al-wikalah): A contract by which one person appoints another to act on his behalf in a permissible matter.
عزل (azl): Dismissal or termination of the agent's authority.
مطبق (mutbiq): Continuous and permanent; used for insanity (جنون مطبق) that never lifts.
اللحاق بدار الحرب (al-ilhaq bi-dar al-harb): Joining enemy territory as an apostate; a legal cause for termination of agency and other transactions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), what is the effect of a woman's apostasy on her agency?
A) Her agency is void immediately upon apostasy.
B) Her agency is not void unless she joins dar al-harb and a judge declares it.
C) Her agency is void only if she appoints an agent for marriage.
D) Her agency becomes suspended until she returns to Islam.

Key Takeaway
Agency in Hanafi fiqh is voided automatically by five events: death, permanent insanity, apostasy with judicial declaration of joining dar al-harb, dissolution of partnership, and legal incapacity of the principal, with an exception for debt collection and bai' al-wafa.

Termination of Agency by Death and Insanity with Exception for Bai' al-Wafa'
Opens the section on termination of agency with rulings on insanity and death

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general rule that agency terminates upon the principal's death or insanity and identify the exception for bai' al-wafa'.

Core Idea
Agency terminates automatically on death or insanity except in bai' al-wafa'.

This lesson examines when and how agency (wakala) ends. The classical Hanafi position holds that the death of the principal or agent, or the onset of insanity, immediately voids the agency—even if the other party does not know. However, there is a notable exception for bai' al-wafa' (the sale of wafa'), a transaction similar to a mortgage, where the agent's role continues to protect the buyer's interest.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
The passage states that agency is voided by death of the principal (and by analogy, agent) and by insanity. Notice that this termination is automatic and does not require knowledge.
2
Recognize the exception
The exception is bai' al-wafa'. The author cites Jami' al-Fusulayn: a valid sale by agency continues even after the principal dies.
Bai' al-wafa' is a conditional sale effectively serving as a mortgage.
3
Understand the rationale
In bai' al-wafa', the buyer's right is tied to the property, so the agent's role persists to protect that right.
4
Apply the rule about insanity
Continuous insanity terminates agency; recovery does not reinstate it.
This applies to both principal and agent.
5
Distinguish the authority level
This is the zahir al-riwayah position (apparent madhhab). Note that other schools may not share this exception.
The author states 'al-madhhab al-zahir' indicating the relied-upon view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الظاهر موكلاً كان أو وكيلاً ومقتضاه أنه لو أفاق بعد جنونه مطبقاً لا تعود وكالته . ثم اعلم أن الوكالة تبطل بموت الموكل إلا في بيع الوفاء. قال في جامع الفصولين: باعه جائزاً بوكالة ثم مات موكله لا ينعزل بموته الوكيل ا هـ . والبيع الجائز هو بيع الوفاء اصطلاحاً.
The apparent madhhab [position] is, whether principal or agent, and its implication is that if he recovers after continuous insanity, his agency does not return. Then know that agency is voided by the death of the principal except in bai' al-wafa'. He said in Jami' al-Fusulayn: He sold it validly by agency then his principal died - his agent is not removed by his death. And the valid sale is bai' al-wafa' terminologically.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with reasoning from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, commenting on Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The author states the relied-upon (zahir al-riwayah) position: agency terminates upon the death of the principal, regardless of whether the death is known to the agent. This is a ruling. The exception is bai' al-wafa' (sale of wafa'), where the agent remains in effect despite the principal's death. This is because bai' al-wafa' is a collateral sale (in the sense of a mortgage), so the buyer has a right that continues. The author cites Jami' al-Fusulayn for this exception. The passage also covers insanity: if the principal or agent becomes insane and then recovers after continuous insanity, the agency does not automatically return. This is because the original termination was complete.

Key Terms
بيع الوفاء (bai' al-wafa'): A sale with the condition that the seller can repurchase upon returning the price; treated as a mortgage in effect.
الوكالة (al-wakala): Agency; a contract where one person delegates another to perform a legal act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does agency in bai' al-wafa' not terminate upon the principal's death?
A) Because the agent is also the buyer
B) Because bai' al-wafa' is a collateral transaction where the buyer has a right that continues
C) Because the principal's heirs automatically become principals
D) Because the agent's death also does not terminate it

Key Takeaway
Agency automatically ends upon death or insanity, except in bai' al-wafa' where the agent's authority continues to safeguard the buyer's equity.

Termination of Agency by Incapacity and Interdiction: Exceptions for Debt and Deposit Agents
Ruling on termination of agency by incapacity and interdiction, with exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish which types of agency are terminated by the principal's incapacity or interdiction and which are not, and apply the rule that continuance requires the same conditions as initiation.

Core Idea
Agency in contracts/lawsuits ends with principal's incapacity; agents for debt or deposit remain.

This lesson examines when an agency ends due to the principal's loss of capacity. The general rule is that incapacity or interdiction voids the agency, but only for agents handling contracts and lawsuits. Special agents for collecting debts or receiving deposits continue because the principal's incapacity does not prevent fulfilling existing obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the termination of agency upon the principal's incapacity or interdiction. The ruling is that it terminates for agents in contracts and lawsuits, but not for agents appointed to pay/collect debts or receive deposits.
The general rule has a clear exception.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is talil (reasoning): agency depends on the principal's command, which is voided by incapacity. However, for debt and deposit, the command remains effective for completion because interdiction only prevents new transactions.
The author cites Kafi al-Hakim for the exception.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The legal link is that the condition for agency (a valid command) must persist. Incapacity voids the command for future acts, but existing obligations (debt/deposit) are not new transactions.
This is a nuanced application of the principle.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
The text does not name a specific opponent, but the restriction implies disagreement with those who hold all agencies terminate.
The Hanafi position is that exceptions are valid.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The mufta bihi is the exception for debt and deposit agents, as per Kafi al-Hakim and the author's fatwa on the nazir case.
The rule 'what is required for initiation is required for continuance' is applied.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وعجز موكله لو مكاتباً وحجره لو مأذونا لما ذكرنا أن قيام الوكالة يعتمد قيام الأمر وقد بطل بالحجر والعجز علم أو لم يعلم أطلقه وهو مقيد بما إذا كان وكيلاً في العقود والخصومات، وأما الوكيل في قضاء الدين واقتضائه فلا ينعزل بهما لأنهما يوجبان الحجر عن إنشاء التصرف لا عن قضاء الدين واقتضائه فكذا لا يوجب عزل وكيله، وكذا الوكيل بقبض الوديعة لم ينعزل بعجزه وحجره كما في كافي الحاكم ولا تعود الوكالة بكتابة موكله وإذنه . وقد حصر المؤلف عزل وكيلهما بهما ويعزل الموكل أخذاً من عموم بطلانها بعزل الموكل، فأفاد أن المولى لو عزل وكيل العبد المأذون له لم ينعزل لأنه كالحجر الخاص. ولو أعتق العبد بعد ما وكله سيده أو طلقها ثلاثاً بعد ما وكلها لم ينعزلا ، وإن باع العبد فإن رضي المشتري أن يكون العبد على وكالته فهو وكيل وإن لم يرض بذلك لم يجبر على الوكالة؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم. وهو يقتضي أن توكيل عبد الغير موقوف على رضا السيد وقد سبق إطلاق جوازه لأنه لا عهدة عليه في ذلك إلا أن يقال إنه من باب استخدام عبد الغير وقد سئلت عن ناظر وكل وكيلاً في أمر الوقف ثم عزله القاضي هل ينعزل وكيله بعزله؟ فأجبت بأنه ينعزل أخذاً من قولهم هنا يشترط لدوامها ما يشترط لابتدائها والله أعلم.
His statement: (and the incapacity of his principal if he is a mukatab, and his interdiction if he is a ma'dhun) because we mentioned that the validity of agency depends on the validity of the command, and it has become void by interdiction and incapacity, whether known or not. He gave it absolutely, and it is restricted to when he is an agent in contracts and lawsuits. As for the agent for paying a debt and collecting it, he is not removed by them because they necessitate interdiction from initiating transactions, not from paying and collecting debt; so likewise, it does not necessitate removal of his agent. Similarly, the agent for receiving a deposit is not removed by his incapacity and interdiction, as in Kafi al-Hakim. And agency does not return by the writing (of a contract) of his principal or his permission. And the author limited the removal of the agent of both to these two (incapacity and interdiction), and the principal removes [the agent] by taking from the general nullification by the principal's removal. So it indicates that if the master removes the agent of the authorized slave, he is not removed because it is like a specific interdiction. If the master frees the slave after appointing him as agent, or divorces her three times after appointing her, they are not removed. If he sells the slave, then if the buyer consents to the slave remaining as agent, he is an agent; if he does not consent, he is not forced to agency. This is in Kafi al-Hakim. And it implies that appointing another's slave as agent is contingent on the master's consent, and previously the permissibility was stated absolutely because there is no liability on him in that, unless it is said that it is from the category of using another's slave. And I was asked about a nazir (supervisor) who appointed an agent for an endowment matter, then the qadi removed him (the nazir); does his agent become removed by his removal? I answered that he is removed, taking from their statement here: 'For its continuance, what is required for its initiation is required.' And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage continues the commentary on agency termination by incapacity (عجز) and interdiction (حجر). The author clarifies that such termination applies only to an agent who acts in contracts and lawsuits. For an agent appointed to pay or collect a debt, or to receive a deposit, the agency continues because interdiction prevents new transactions but not completion of existing obligations. The text then discusses specific cases: if a master appoints his authorized slave as an agent and then removes him, the removal is ineffective because the master's removal is like a specific interdiction that does not terminate the slave's original permission. If the master frees the slave or divorces his wife (who was appointed agent), the agency continues. If the master sells the slave, the new owner may accept or reject the agency. This leads to the principle that appointing another person's slave as agent requires the owner's consent. The author then relates a fatwa: if a nazir (endowment supervisor) is removed by a qadi, his agent is also removed, following the rule that the same conditions for initiating agency are required for its continuation.

Key Terms
مكاتب (mukatab): A slave who has entered a contract of manumission with his master, to pay for his freedom.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is an agent for collecting a debt not removed by the principal's interdiction?
A) Because interdiction only prevents initiating new transactions, not completing obligations
B) Because the agent is immune to removal
C) Because the debt belongs to the agent
D) Because interdiction requires a court order

Key Takeaway
Agency in contracts and lawsuits terminates upon principal's incapacity or interdiction, but agencies for debt collection and deposit receipt continue because they involve completing existing obligations.

Termination of Agency by Principal's Own Action
Detailed scenarios of principal's own actions and their effect on agency

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for when a principal's own action terminates the agency and identify which specific actions void the agency and which do not.

Core Idea
A principal's own act voids the agency only if it makes the agent's task impossible.

The general rule in Hanafi fiqh is that an agency (wakalah) is terminated when the principal himself performs the act for which the agent was appointed, because the need for the agency ends. However, this rule is qualified: termination occurs only if the principal's action renders the agent incapable of performing the act. If the agent can still act despite the principal's involvement, the agency continues. This lesson explores a series of scenarios from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq that illustrate this qualification in practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule and its qualifier
Note that the base rule is that the principal's own action voids the agency due to 'end of need' (inqida' al-hajah). Then note the restriction: only when the action renders the agent incapable of acting alongside it.
The key is incapacity of the agent, not any action.
2
Apply to clear-cut scenarios where agency ends
Review scenarios where the principal's act makes the subject matter unavailable: freeing a slave, marrying a woman, buying the item, giving three divorces, khul'. In each, the agent's task becomes impossible.
3
Distinguish scenarios where agency continues
Study cases where the principal's act does not eliminate the agent's ability to act: single divorce with remaining idda, apostasy of husband, sale with rescission by faskh, mortgage, lease, building on land (according to some views). These do not terminate agency.
The distinction hinges on whether the agent can still perform the act later.
4
Analyze special cases: building, planting, aging
Examine the difference between building/planting (considered revocation) and mere plastering/adding a wall (not revocation). Also the case of a slave girl who ages: agency remains for sale, but if ordered to buy, aging prevents?
Building and planting show intent to keep, so agency revoked; aging does not show such intent.
5
Summarize the operative principle
Conclude that the rule is not absolute; it applies only when the principal's act makes the agent's performance impossible or changes the nature of the subject matter in a way that frustrates the agency purpose.
This is a core principle in Hanafi wakalah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتصرفه بنفسه أي يبطل بتصرف الموكل فيما وكل فيه لانقضاء الحاجة. أطلقه وهو مقيد بتصرف يعجز الوكيل عن التصرف معه كما لو وكله بإعتاق عبده أو بكتابته فأعتقه أو كاتبه الموكل بنفسه أو بتزويج امرأة أو بشراء شيء ففعل بنفسه أو بطلاق فطلقها الزوج ثلاثاً أو واحدة فانقضت عدتها أو بالخلع فخالعها بنفسه، وأما ما لا يعجز عنه فلا تبطل به كما لو طلقها واحدة والعدة باقية فللوكيل أن يطلقها أخرى ولو ارتد الزوج وقع طلاق الوكيل عليها ما دامت في العدة والحوقه بمنزلة ،موته ولو وكله بطلاقها فخالعها الزوج وقع طلاق الوكيل في عدتها، ولو وكل بالبيع فباعه الموكل ثم رد عليه بما هو فسخ فالوكيل على وكالته، وإن رد بما لا يكون فسخاً لا تعود الوكالة كما لو وكله في هبة شيء ثم وهبه الموكل ثم رجع في هبته لم يكن للوكيل الهبة، ولو وكله بالبيع ثم رهنه الموكل أو أجره فسلمه فهو على وكالته في ظاهر الرواية، ولو وكله أن يؤجر داره ثم أجرها الموكل بنفسه ثم انفسخت الإجارة يعود على وكالته ؛ كذا في القنية . وفي البزازية ولو وكله ببيع داره ثم بنى فيها فهو رجوع عنها عند الإمام ومحمد لأن التجصيص والوصية بمنزلة الوكالة، وكذا لو ببيع أرضه ثم غرس فيها بخلاف ما إذا وكله ببيع أرض وزرع فيبيع الوكيل الأرض دون الزرع لأن البناء والغرس يقصد بهما القرار لا الزرع أمره بشراء دار وهي أرض بيضاء فبنى فيها ليس له أن يشتريها بعده، ولو كانت مبنية فزاد فيها حائطاً أو جصصها له البيع. ببيع وصيفة وهي شابة فصارت عجوزاً فالوكالة على حالها بخلاف ما إذا أمره بشراء - وكله وكله فالمشتري مرتهن قوله : ( عزل وكيلهما بهما) أي الأجر والعجز قوله : (إلا أن يقال الخ) إذا كان من باب الاستخدام لعبد الغير يتوقف على رضا سيده لأنه لا يملك منافعه تأمل. قوله : (لأن التجصيص) هكذا في أغلب النسخ وفي نسخة لا التجصيص» بلا النافية وقوله والوصية» مبتدأ خبره ما بعده.
His statement: (and his own action) meaning it is voided by the principal's action in the matter for which he was appointed due to the end of need. He gave it absolutely, and it is restricted to an action that renders the agent incapable of acting alongside it, such as if he appointed him to free his slave or write a kitabah, then the principal himself freed him or wrote a kitabah; or to marry a woman, then he himself married her; or to buy something, then he himself bought it; or to divorce, then the husband divorced her three times or once and her idda ended; or to khul', then he himself khala'a her. As for what does not render him incapable, it does not void, such as if he divorced her once and the idda remains, so the agent may divorce her another time. If the husband apostatizes, the agent's divorce of her occurs as long as she is in idda, and his joining dar al-harb is like his death. If he appointed him to divorce her and the husband khala'a her, the agent's divorce occurs in her idda. If he appointed him to sell and the principal sold it, then it was returned to him by a [transaction that is] a rescission, the agent remains on his agency; if it was returned by something not a rescission, the agency does not return, as if he appointed him to give a gift, then the principal gave it as a gift and then revoked the gift, the agent does not have [authority] to give it. If he appointed him to sell, then the principal mortgaged it or leased it and delivered it, he remains on his agency in the apparent narration. If he appointed him to lease his house, then the principal himself leased it, then the lease was dissolved, he returns to his agency. This is in al-Qunyah. In al-Bazzaziyyah: If he appointed him to sell his house then he built in it, it is a revocation according to Imam [Abu Hanifa] and Muhammad because plastering and bequest are like agency; similarly if he appointed him to sell his land then he planted it, contrary to if he appointed him to sell land and crop, then the agent sells the land without the crop, because building and planting are intended for settlement, not planting. If he ordered him to buy a house and it was empty land, then he built in it, he may not buy it afterwards. If it was built and he added a wall or plastered it, he may sell it. For selling a slave girl who was young and became old, the agency remains as it was, contrary to if he ordered him to buy. (Then corrupt text: 'وكله وكله فالمشتري مرتهن'). His statement: (removal of his agent by both) meaning by seizure and incapacity. His statement: (unless it is said etc.) if it is from the category of using another's slave, it depends on the master's consent because he does not own his services. Reflect. His statement: (because plastering) this is in most copies, and in some copies 'not plastering' with the negative, and his statement 'and bequest' is the subject, its predicate is what follows.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This long passage covers many scenarios of when the principal's own action terminates the agency. The general rule: the agency ends if the principal's action eliminates the need for the agency (i.e., makes the subject matter unavailable). The key qualifier: the action must render the agent incapable of acting on the matter. For example, if the principal himself frees the slave the agent was appointed to free, the agency ends because the slave is already freed. If the principal divorces his wife only once, leaving idda, the agent can still give a second divorce. The passage also covers scenarios of apostasy, khul', sale with rescission, mortgage after appointment, and changes in the property (building, planting, aging of a slave girl). Some actions (like mortgaging) do not terminate the agency in the apparent narration. Building or planting on land intended for sale is considered a revocation by Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because it shows intent to keep the property. The passage ends with some marginal notes that are textually corrupt; they comment on earlier parts of the text.

Key Terms
انقضاء الحاجة (inqida' al-hajah): The end of the need for which the agency was created; trigger for termination if the principal himself fulfills it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a principal appoints an agent to sell his house, then later mortgages the house and delivers it to the mortgagee, what happens to the agency?
A) The agency is voided immediately
B) The agency continues because the mortgage does not prevent sale
C) The agency continues only if the mortgagee consents
D) The agency becomes suspended until the mortgage is lifted

Key Takeaway
The agency ends only when the principal's action makes it impossible for the agent to act.

Nullification of Agency by Principal's Action (Condition of Incapacitation)
Expansion of principal's action nullifying agency, with condition of incapacitation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that the principal's own act nullifies the agency only if it prevents the agent from performing, and apply this rule to examples such as building, planting, and mortgaging.

Core Idea
A principal's act nullifies agency only if it disables the agent—mere action is not enough.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq refines the general understanding that a principal's own action automatically ends agency. The Hanafi school conditions nullification on the agent being incapacitated, preserving agency where the agent can still act. This distinction is key to applying the law consistently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
State the ruling when the principal performs the act himself: the agency is nullified only if the agent is prevented from acting.
The text says 'مقيد بتصرف يعجز الوكيل عن التصرف معه'.
2
Apply the condition to clear examples
List actions that nullify: freeing, writing kitaba, marrying, buying, divorcing ending iddah, khul'. These fulfill the need.
3
Identify actions that do not nullify
Mortgaging or leasing does not nullify because the agent can still sell the mortgaged property subject to the encumbrance.
This is from the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah).
4
Analyze building and planting as retraction
Building or planting is considered a retraction of agency for sale according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani, because it indicates the principal intends to keep the property.
Plastering (tajsis) is similar to building.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
The text records an ikhtilaf: Imam and Muhammad treat building/planting as retraction; there may be a differing view from Abu Yusuf (not mentioned).
The operative ruling (mufta bihi) is the opinion of Imam and Muhammad.

كتاب الوكالة باب عزل الوكيل
الوديعة لم ينعزل بعجزه وحجره كما في كافي الحاكم ولا تعود الوكالة بكتابة موكله وإذنه . وقد حصر المؤلف عزل وكيلهما بهما ويعزل الموكل أخذاً من عموم بطلانها بعزل الموكل، فأفاد أن المولى لو عزل وكيل العبد المأذون له لم ينعزل لأنه كالحجر الخاص. ولو أعتق العبد بعد ما وكله سيده أو طلقها ثلاثاً بعد ما وكلها لم ينعزلا ، وإن باع العبد فإن رضي المشتري أن يكون العبد على وكالته فهو وكيل وإن لم يرض بذلك لم يجبر على الوكالة؛ كذا في كافي الحاكم. وهو يقتضي أن توكيل عبد الغير موقوف على رضا السيد وقد سبق إطلاق جوازه لأنه لا عهدة عليه في ذلك إلا أن يقال إنه من باب استخدام عبد الغير وقد سئلت عن ناظر وكل وكيلاً في أمر الوقف ثم عزله القاضي هل ينعزل وكيله بعزله؟ فأجبت بأنه ينعزل أخذاً من قولهم هنا يشترط لدوامها ما يشترط لابتدائها والله أعلم.
قوله : (وتصرفه بنفسه أي يبطل بتصرف الموكل فيما وكل فيه لانقضاء الحاجة. أطلقه وهو مقيد بتصرف يعجز الوكيل عن التصرف معه كما لو وكله بإعتاق عبده أو بكتابته فأعتقه أو كاتبه الموكل بنفسه أو بتزويج امرأة أو بشراء شيء ففعل بنفسه أو بطلاق فطلقها الزوج ثلاثاً أو واحدة فانقضت عدتها أو بالخلع فخالعها بنفسه، وأما ما لا يعجز عنه فلا تبطل به كما لو طلقها واحدة والعدة باقية فللوكيل أن يطلقها أخرى ولو ارتد الزوج وقع طلاق الوكيل عليها ما دامت في العدة والحوقه بمنزلة موته ولو وكله بطلاقها فخالعها الزوج وقع طلاق الوكيل في عدتها، ولو وكل بالبيع فباعه الموكل ثم رد عليه بما هو فسخ فالوكيل على وكالته، وإن رد بما لا يكون فسخاً لا تعود الوكالة كما لو وكله في هبة شيء ثم وهبه الموكل ثم رجع في هبته لم يكن للوكيل الهبة، ولو وكله بالبيع ثم رهنه الموكل أو أجره فسلمه فهو على وكالته في ظاهر الرواية، ولو وكله أن يؤجر داره ثم أجرها الموكل بنفسه ثم انفسخت الإجارة يعود على وكالته ؛ كذا في القنية . وفي البزازية ولو وكله ببيع داره ثم بنى فيها فهو رجوع عنها عند الإمام ومحمد لأن التجصيص والوصية بمنزلة الوكالة، وكذا لو ببيع أرضه ثم غرس فيها بخلاف ما إذا وكله ببيع أرض وزرع فيبيع الوكيل الأرض دون الزرع لأن البناء والغرس يقصد بهما القرار لا الزرع أمره بشراء دار وهي أرض بيضاء فبنى فيها ليس له أن يشتريها بعده، ولو كانت مبنية فزاد فيها حائطاً أو جصصها له البيع. ببيع وصيفة وهي شابة فصارت عجوزاً فالوكالة على حالها بخلاف ما إذا أمره بشراء [؟] وكله وكله فالمشتري مرتهن قوله : ( عزل وكيلهما بهما) أي الأجر والعجز قوله : (إلا أن يقال الخ) إذا كان من باب الاستخدام لعبد الغير يتوقف على رضا سيده لأنه لا يملك منافعه تأمل.
قوله : (لأن التجصيص) هكذا في أغلب النسخ وفي نسخة لا التجصيص بلا النافية وقوله والوصية مبتدأ خبره ما بعده.
Book of Agency, Chapter of Dismissal of the Agent. The deposit is not dismissed by his inability and his restriction as in Kafi al-Hakim. And the agency does not return by the writing of his principal and his permission. The author restricted the dismissal of both agents with both of them. And the principal dismisses, taken from the generality of its nullification by the dismissal of the principal. So he indicated that if the master dismisses the agent of the permitted slave, he is not dismissed because it is like a special restriction. And if the slave is freed after his master appointed him, or he divorced her three times after he appointed her, they are not dismissed. And if the slave is sold, if the buyer is pleased that the slave remain on his agency, he is an agent; if he is not pleased, he is not forced upon agency; as in Kafi al-Hakim. And it requires that appointment of another's slave is suspended upon the satisfaction of the master, and previously the absolute permissibility has been mentioned because there is no liability upon him in that, except if it is said that it is from the category of using another's slave. And I was asked about a supervisor who appointed an agent in a waqf matter, then the judge dismissed him: is his agent dismissed by his dismissal? I answered that he is dismissed, taken from their statement here: 'What is required for its continuation is what is required for its commencement.' And Allah knows best. His statement: 'And his own action' meaning it is nullified by the action of the principal in what he was appointed for due to the end of need. He made it absolute, but it is restricted to an action that incapacitates the agent from acting with it, such as if he appointed him to free his slave or to write a contract of kitaba, and the principal himself freed or wrote the kitaba; or to marry a woman or buy something, and he did it himself; or to divorce, so the husband divorced her three times or once and her iddah ended; or to khul', so he khala'd her himself. As for what does not incapacitate, it is not nullified by it, such as if he divorced her once and the iddah remains, so the agent may divorce her another time. And if the husband apostatizes, the agent's divorce of her takes effect as long as she is in iddah, and his apostasy is like his death. And if he appointed him to divorce her, and the husband khala'd her, the agent's divorce takes effect in her iddah. And if he appointed him to sell, and the principal sold it, then he returned it in a way that is a rescission, the agent remains on his agency. And if he returned it in a way that is not a rescission, the agency does not return, such as if he appointed him to give something as a gift, and the principal gave it as a gift, then retracted his gift, the agent does not have the gift. And if he appointed him to sell, then the principal mortgaged it or leased it and delivered it, he remains on his agency in the apparent narration. And if he appointed him to lease his house, then the principal himself leased it, then the lease was rescinded, he returns to his agency; as in al-Qunyah. And in al-Bazzaziyyah: if he appointed him to sell his house, then he built in it, it is a retraction from it according to Imam and Muhammad, because plastering and bequest are like agency. Similarly, if he appointed him to sell his land, then he planted in it, unlike if he appointed him to sell land and crop, the agent sells the land without the crop, because building and planting intend permanence, not crop. He ordered him to buy a house, and it was empty land, so he built in it, he does not have the right to buy it afterwards. And if it was built, and he added a wall or plastered it, he has the right to sell. He appointed him to sell a slave-girl who was young, then she became old, the agency remains as it was, unlike if he ordered him to buy [???] and [???] so the buyer is a mortgagee. His statement: 'Dismissal of both agents with both' meaning the building and inability. His statement: 'except if it is said etc.' if it is from the category of using another's slave, it depends on the satisfaction of his master, because he does not own his benefits. Consider. His statement: 'Because plastering' is like this in most copies, and in a copy 'not plastering' with the negative la, and his statement 'and bequest' is the subject and its predicate follows.
Source pages p. 324

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is a commentary on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq in the chapter on dismissal of the agent. It discusses several rulings regarding when an agency is nullified. The passage begins by noting that a deposit is not dismissed by the agent's incapacity or restriction, as mentioned in Kafi al-Hakim. Also, agency does not automatically return if the principal writes or permits something. The author then addresses the dismissal by the principal. Importantly, the principal's dismissal of an agent appointed by a master over his slave is ineffective because it is like a special restriction (hajr khas). Similarly, if the master frees the slave or divorces the slave-wife after appointing them as agents, they are not dismissed. If the slave is sold, the buyer may choose to keep the slave as agent; if not, he cannot be forced. This implies that appointing another's slave as agent is suspended on the master's consent. The passage then discusses the principal's own action: the agency is nullified if the principal performs the task himself, but only if that action prevents the agent from acting. For example, if the principal frees the slave, writes kitaba, marries, buys, or divorces in a way that ends the need, the agency ends. If the principal divorces once but iddah remains, the agent can still divorce another time. Apostasy of the husband is like death. Various examples follow: if the principal sells and then the sale is rescinded in a way that is a true rescission (faskh), the agent remains; if it is not a true rescission, agency does not return. Mortgaging or leasing does not nullify agency in the apparent narration. Building or plastering by the principal is considered a retraction according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Muhammad al-Shaybani. However, if the land was empty and the principal built, the agent cannot buy it afterwards; if it was built and the principal added, the agent may still sell. Change in the condition of the slave-girl (becoming old) does not nullify agency. The passage ends with textual notes on the variant reading of 'al-tajsis'.

Key Terms
العزل (al-'azl): Dismissal of the agent by the principal, which nullifies the agency.
التجصيص (al-tajsis): Plastering a wall; considered a form of retraction of the agency to sell.
الوكالة (al-wakalah): A contract of agency where one appoints another to act on his behalf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following principal actions does NOT nullify the agency according to the apparent narration in this passage?
A) Building a wall on the house the agent is to sell
B) Mortgaging the house the agent is to sell
C) Selling the house himself
D) Giving the house as a gift and the recipient accepts

Key Takeaway
A principal's own action nullifies agency only if it prevents the agent from acting; building/planting is a special case of retraction.

Effect of Change in Agent's Status on Agency (Freedom, Sale, Apostasy, Dismissal)
Expansion on how changes in agent's status (freedom, sale, apostasy, dismissal) affect agency.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which changes in the agent's status nullify agency and which do not, applying the Hanafi principles of continuity and consent.

Core Idea
Changes in the agent's status do not automatically end agency; the agent's capacity and the master's consent are key.

Agency can survive many changes in the agent's personal status, such as manumission, sale, or apostasy, unless the change fundamentally undermines the relationship. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies these nuances, protecting the agent's authority in most circumstances.

Guided Path
1
State the general principle
Agency is not automatically nullified by changes in the agent's status unless the change directly contradicts the basis of the agency.
2
Apply to manumission of a slave agent
If the master frees a slave who was appointed as an agent during slavery, the agency continues; freedom does not nullify it.
Text: 'ولو أعتق العبد بعد ما وكله سيده لم ينعزل'.
3
Apply to sale of the slave agent
If a slave agent is sold by the master, the buyer may choose to keep the slave as agent (if pleased) or refuse (then agency ends).
The buyer cannot be forced to accept the agency.
4
Apply to apostasy of the agent
Apostasy of the agent is treated like death: it does not retroactively nullify prior acts, and the agent's actions during iddah remain valid (e.g., divorce).
Text: 'لو ارتد الزوج وقع طلاق الوكيل عليها ما دامت في العدة'.
5
Apply to dismissal by judge in waqf
If a judge dismisses a supervisor, the supervisor's agent is also dismissed, based on the maxim: 'What is required for its continuation is what is required for its commencement'.
This is an extension of the principle that agency depends on the principal's authority.

Source Text
